## Idea

2-element types are types that are merely equivalent to the standard 2-element type `Fin 2`.

## Definition

### The condition that a type has two elements

<pre class="Agda"><a id="has-two-elements-Prop"></a><a id="4304" href="univalent-combinatorics.2-element-types.html#4304" class="Function">has-two-elements-Prop</a> <a id="4326" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="4328" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="4329" href="univalent-combinatorics.2-element-types.html#4329" class="Bound">l</a> <a id="4331" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="4333" href="Agda.Primitive.html#597" class="Postulate">Level</a><a id="4338" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="4340" class="Symbol">‚Üí</a> <a id="4342" href="foundation-core.universe-levels.html#235" class="Primitive">UU</a> <a id="4345" href="univalent-combinatorics.2-element-types.html#4329" class="Bound">l</a> <a id="4347" class="Symbol">‚Üí</a> <a id="4349" href="foundation-core.propositions.html#1393" class="Function">UU-Prop</a> <a id="4357" href="univalent-combinatorics.2-element-types.html#4329" class="Bound">l</a>

## Properties

### The condition of having two elements is closed under equivalences

<pre class="Agda"><a id="5568" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="5575" href="univalent-combinatorics.2-element-types.html#5575" class="Module">_</a>
  <a id="5579" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="5580" href="univalent-combinatorics.2-element-types.html#5580" class="Bound">l1</a> <a id="5583" href="univalent-combinatorics.2-element-types.html#5583" class="Bound">l2</a> <a id="5586" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="5588" href="Agda.Primitive.html#597" class="Postulate">Level</a><a id="5593" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="5595" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="5596" href="univalent-combinatorics.2-element-types.html#5596" class="Bound">X</a> <a id="5598" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="5600" href="foundation-core.universe-levels.html#235" class="Primitive">UU</a> <a id="5603" href="univalent-combinatorics.2-element-types.html#5580" class="Bound">l1</a><a id="5605" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="5607" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="5608" href="univalent-combinatorics.2-element-types.html#5608" class="Bound">Y</a> <a id="5610" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="5612" href="foundation-core.universe-levels.html#235" class="Primitive">UU</a> <a id="5615" href="univalent-combinatorics.2-element-types.html#5583" class="Bound">l2</a><a id="5617" class="Symbol">}</a>
  <a id="5621" class="Keyword">where</a>

</pre>
#### If `X` is a 2-element type, then evaluating an equivalence `Fin 2 ‚âÉ X` at `0` is an equivalence

#### The type of pointed 2-element types of any universe level is contractible

<pre class="Agda"><a id="13743" class="Keyword">abstract</a>

            <a id="20618" class="Symbol">(</a> <a id="20620" class="Symbol">Œª</a> <a id="20622" href="univalent-combinatorics.2-element-types.html#20622" class="Bound">e</a> <a id="20624" class="Symbol">‚Üí</a> <a id="20626" href="foundation.double-negation.html#1033" class="Function">intro-dn</a> <a id="20635" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="20636" href="univalent-combinatorics.2-element-types.html#20360" class="Bound">l</a><a id="20637" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="20639" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="20640" href="foundation-core.equivalences.html#1821" class="Function">map-equiv</a> <a id="20650" href="univalent-combinatorics.2-element-types.html#20622" class="Bound">e</a> <a id="20652" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="20653" href="univalent-combinatorics.standard-finite-types.html#6795" class="Function">zero-Fin</a> <a id="20662" class="Number">1</a><a id="20663" class="Symbol">))))</a>
          <a id="20678" class="Symbol">(</a> <a id="20680" href="univalent-combinatorics.2-element-types.html#20363" class="Bound">d</a> <a id="20682" href="univalent-combinatorics.2-element-types.html#20416" class="Bound">X</a><a id="20683" class="Symbol">))</a>
</pre>

### There can't be three distinct elements in a 2-element type

<pre class="Agda"><a id="30785" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="30792" href="univalent-combinatorics.2-element-types.html#30792" class="Module">_</a>
